</ul></div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class=col><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/compilation>Compilation</a></ul></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2017-10-keeping-up-with-the-jsons>Keeping up with the JSONs</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2017-10-01T00:00:00.000Z>October 1, 2017</time></div></header><div class=markdown><p>Incoming webhooks can do it. <a class="" href=/interactivity/implementing-slash-commands>Slash commands</a> and <a class="" href=/legacy/legacy-messaging/legacy-making-messages-interactive>interactive messages</a> speak it fluently. The message builder knows no other format. But, until now, <a class="" href=/reference/methods/chat.postMessage><code>chat.postMessage</code></a> stubbornly refused to understand your messages composed in impeccable JSON.</p>
<p>Finally, Slack allows you to send JSON to <a href=#methods class="">a wide selection</a> of write-based <a class="" href=/apis/web-api/>Web API</a> methods. Additionally, now you can better separate concerns when presenting your credentials to Slack.</div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class="col col--9"><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/new-feature>New feature</a></ul></div><div class="col text--right col--3"><a aria-label="Read more about Keeping up with the JSONs" href=/changelog/2017-10-keeping-up-with-the-jsons><b>Read more</b></a></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2017-10-making-rtm-presence-subscription-only>Making RTM presence subscription only</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2017-10-01T00:00:00.000Z>October 1, 2017</time></div></header><div class=markdown><div class="theme-admonition theme-admonition-warning admonition_xJq3 alert alert--warning"><div class=admonitionHeading_Gvgb><span class=admonitionIcon_Rf37><svg viewBox="0 0 16 16"><path fill-rule=evenodd d="M8.893 1.5c-.183-.31-.52-.5-.887-.5s-.703.19-.886.5L.138 13.499a.98.98 0 0 0 0 1.001c.193.31.53.501.886.501h13.964c.367 0 .704-.19.877-.5a1.03 1.03 0 0 0 .01-1.002L8.893 1.5zm.133 11.497H6.987v-2.003h2.039v2.003zm0-3.004H6.987V5.987h2.039v4.006z"/></svg></span>RTM API Presence is now only available via subscription.</div><div class=admonitionContent_BuS1><p>As of January 2018, <a class="" href=/reference/events/presence_change><code>presence_change</code></a> events are not dispatched without <a class="" href=/apis/web-api/user-presence-and-status><em>presence subscriptions</em></a> established with <a class="" href=/reference/events/presence_sub><code>presence_sub</code></a>. Relatedly, current user presence status is no longer communicated in <a class="" href=/reference/methods/rtm.start><code>rtm.start</code></a>. <a class="" href=/changelog/2018-01-presence-present-and-future>Learn more</a>.</div></div>
<p><strong>Beginning November 15, 2017, the RTM API's <a class="" href=/reference/events/presence_change><code>presence_sub</code></a> event will be available via presence subscription only.</strong></p>
<p><a class="" href=/changelog/2017-06-batch-presence-and-presence-subscriptions>Back in June</a>, we introduced new ways to track user presence and the <a class="" href=/reference/events/presence_change><code>presence_change</code></a> event in the <a class="" href=/legacy/legacy-rtm-api>RTM API</a>.</p>
<p>Dispatching presence events for all users in a workspace is an expensive operation for Slack. A flood of presence events from large workspaces can also disrupt your app's ability to process more useful, timely messages.</p>
<p>By subscribing only to the presence events your app needs to provide presence-dependent functionality, you can reduce unnecessary websocket traffic.</div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class="col col--9"><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/breaking-change>Breaking change</a><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/announcement>Announcement</a></ul></div><div class="col text--right col--3"><a aria-label="Read more about Making RTM presence subscription only" href=/changelog/2017-10-making-rtm-presence-subscription-only><b>Read more</b></a></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2017/10/01/members-array-truncating>The members array is being truncated</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2017-10-01T00:00:00.000Z>October 1, 2017</time></div></header><div class=markdown><p>Arrays of <code>members</code> found in API methods will become truncated beginning December 1, 2017.</p>
<div class="theme-admonition theme-admonition-warning admonition_xJq3 alert alert--warning"><div class=admonitionHeading_Gvgb><span class=admonitionIcon_Rf37><svg viewBox="0 0 16 16"><path fill-rule=evenodd d="M8.893 1.5c-.183-.31-.52-.5-.887-.5s-.703.19-.886.5L.138 13.499a.98.98 0 0 0 0 1.001c.193.31.53.501.886.501h13.964c.367 0 .704-.19.877-.5a1.03 1.03 0 0 0 .01-1.002L8.893 1.5zm.133 11.497H6.987v-2.003h2.039v2.003zm0-3.004H6.987V5.987h2.039v4.006z"/></svg></span>The maximum number of results found in <code>members</code> continues to decrease regularly</div><div class=admonitionContent_BuS1><p>As of March 2018, the limit is set to 500 results. Use <a class="" href=/reference/methods/conversations.members><code>conversations.members</code></a> for channels with large memberships.</div></div>
<p>Initially, Slack will limit <code>members</code> to the first 1,500 users and then gradually lower the number of users returned. You should expect API methods will cease returning <code>members</code> entirely at some point in the future. If you rely on the <code>members</code> array, you should instead begin using <a class="" href=/reference/methods/conversations.members><code>conversations.members</code></a> for a full list of members.</p>
<p>As Slack teams continue to grow in size, returning the full <code>members</code> array in these methods is no longer practical or performant, for the Slack APIs or developers. The <code>conversations.members</code> method will allow you to request a list of members at a time that makes sense for your app and should keep these method calls nice and zippy.</div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class="col col--9"><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/breaking-change>Breaking change</a><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/announcement>Announcement</a></ul></div><div class="col text--right col--3"><a aria-label="Read more about The members array is being truncated" href=/changelog/2017/10/01/members-array-truncating><b>Read more</b></a></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2017/09/01/locale-locale-locale>Locale locale locale</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2017-09-01T00:00:00.000Z>September 1, 2017</time></div></header><div class=markdown><p>Slack now supports multiple languages, and your app or integration can too.</p>
<p>Add a <code>locale</code> in <a class="" href=/reference/objects/user-object>user</a> and <a class="" href=/reference/objects/conversation-object>conversation</a> by using the <code>include_locale=true</code> parameter when requesting a bundle of Web API methods supporting it.</p>
<p>The locale field is a string containing a <a href=https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IETF_language_tag target=_blank rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">IETF language code</a>, such as <code>en-US</code>. <code>fr-FR</code>, <code>es-ES</code>, or <code>de-DE</code>, and other future values.</p>
<p>We now support <code>include_locale</code> on these methods. Opt-in to receive a <code>locale</code> field in user profiles or the <code>locale</code> of a conversation.</p>
<ul>
<li class=""><a class="" href=/reference/methods/conversations.info><code>conversations.info</code></a></li>
<li class=""><a class="" href=/reference/methods/rtm.start><code>rtm.start</code></a></li>
<li class=""><a class="" href=/reference/methods/users.info><code>users.info</code></a></li>
<li class=""><a class="" href=/reference/methods/users.list><code>users.list</code></a></li>
</ul>
<p>If you don't include the parameter, no <code>locale</code> will be provided. It's opt-in.</p>
<p>You'll also see locale information changes in related user profile change events in the RTM and Events APIs.</div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class="col col--9"><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/new-feature>New feature</a></ul></div><div class="col text--right col--3"><a aria-label="Read more about Locale locale locale" href=/changelog/2017/09/01/locale-locale-locale><b>Read more</b></a></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2017-09-the-one-about-usernames>The one about usernames</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2017-09-01T00:00:00.000Z>September 1, 2017</time></div></header><div class=markdown><p>Slack is phasing out the <code>@username</code> artifact in favor of the more expressive and flexible concept of <em>display names</em>.</p>
<p>Handles, aliases, call-signs, and usernames — in chat, they all represent the same concept: a way for an individual or entity to indicate a preferred identification noun, in whichever way is appropriate to the apparatus at work.</p>
<p>Users will be even better equipped to present their preferred nomenclature while giving organizations the option to work primarily with so-called <em>real</em> names as suits "the suits."</p>
<p>The transition should be technically "backwards compatible" to you, the developer. But the social ramifications, changes in user behavior, and treatments given in Slack clients will inevitably alter the way your apps approach interpreting, storing, and utilizing the now <em>deprecated</em> <code>name</code> field.</p>
<p>As fellow developers, we know you'll have some feelings about the sunset of <code>@username</code> considering its historical significance in computing, networking, and digital identity. From mainframes to UNIX to BBSes to IRC, maybe you've used the same name for what seems like centuries.</p>
<p>Fly your freak, geek, or mild-mannered flag proudly by just setting your <em>display name</em> to your preferred <code>@username</code>.</div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class="col col--9"><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/breaking-change>Breaking change</a><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/announcement>Announcement</a></ul></div><div class="col text--right col--3"><a aria-label="Read more about The one about usernames" href=/changelog/2017-09-the-one-about-usernames><b>Read more</b></a></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2017-06-batch-presence-and-presence-subscriptions>Batch presence and presence subscriptions</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2017-06-01T00:00:00.000Z>June 1, 2017</time></div></header><div class=markdown><div class="theme-admonition theme-admonition-warning admonition_xJq3 alert alert--warning"><div class=admonitionHeading_Gvgb><span class=admonitionIcon_Rf37><svg viewBox="0 0 16 16"><path fill-rule=evenodd d="M8.893 1.5c-.183-.31-.52-.5-.887-.5s-.703.19-.886.5L.138 13.499a.98.98 0 0 0 0 1.001c.193.31.53.501.886.501h13.964c.367 0 .704-.19.877-.5a1.03 1.03 0 0 0 .01-1.002L8.893 1.5zm.133 11.497H6.987v-2.003h2.039v2.003zm0-3.004H6.987V5.987h2.039v4.006z"/></svg></span>RTM API Presence is now only available via subscription.</div><div class=admonitionContent_BuS1><p>As of January 2018, <a class="" href=/reference/events/presence_change><code>presence_change</code></a> events are not dispatched without <a class="" href=/apis/web-api/user-presence-and-status><em>presence subscriptions</em></a> established with <a class="" href=/reference/events/presence_sub><code>presence_sub</code></a>. Relatedly, current user presence status is no longer communicated in <a class="" href=/reference/methods/rtm.start><code>rtm.start</code></a>. <a class="" href=/changelog/2018-01-presence-present-and-future>Learn more</a>.</div></div>
<p>If you've been developing on Slack for awhile you may have noticed a continued theme with updates we make to the platform and APIs: larger teams and evolving use cases mean previous ways of enumerating collections of data become unwieldy and even problematic.</p>
<p>In this exciting edition of the changelog, I'd like to introduce you to new ways to work with <code>presence_change</code> events in the <a class="" href=/legacy/legacy-rtm-api>RTM API</a>.</p>
<p><strong>If you don't work with the RTM API or don't utilize <code>presence_change</code> events, there's very little of value for you in this changelog.</strong></div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class="col col--9"><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/announcement>Announcement</a></ul></div><div class="col text--right col--3"><a aria-label="Read more about Batch presence and presence subscriptions" href=/changelog/2017-06-batch-presence-and-presence-subscriptions><b>Read more</b></a></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2017/05/01/rethinking-channel-entrance-and-exit-events-and-messages>Rethinking channel entrance and exit events and messages</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2017-05-01T00:00:00.000Z>May 1, 2017</time></div></header><div class=markdown><p>We've long delivered a <a class="" href=/reference/events/message>message subtype event</a> to everyone in a channel as members come and go.</p>
<p>As a <em>message</em>, its main purpose is to communicate facts to <em>users</em> but it was never a very good vehicle for communicating these facts to bots and applications.</p>
<p>We're introducing new, more frugal logic behind when Slack dispatches <a class="" href=/reference/events/message/channel_join><code>message.channel_join</code></a> and <a class="" href=/reference/events/message/channel_leave><code>message.channel_leave</code></a> <a class="" href=/reference/events/message>message subtype</a> events in the <a class="" href=/legacy/legacy-rtm-api>RTM API</a> and <a class="" href=/apis/events-api/>Events API</a>.</p>
<p>If you've relied on these events for programmatic notice when members leave or join a channel, we've got new, strongly structured signals for you to subscribe to and consume instead, <a class="" href=/reference/events/member_joined_channel><code>member_joined_channel</code></a> and <a class="" href=/reference/events/member_left_channel><code>member_left_channel</code></a>.</div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class="col col--9"><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/announcement>Announcement</a></ul></div><div class="col text--right col--3"><a aria-label="Read more about Rethinking channel entrance and exit events and messages" href=/changelog/2017/05/01/rethinking-channel-entrance-and-exit-events-and-messages><b>Read more</b></a></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2017-04-narrowing-email-access>Narrowing email access</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2017-04-01T00:00:00.000Z>April 1, 2017</time></div></header><div class=markdown><p>Back in November 2016, we <a class="" href=/changelog/2016-11-10-addressing-email-addresses>introduced</a> the <code>users:read.email</code> OAuth permission scope, allowing more explicit access to email addresses.</p>
<p>To help developers with the transition, we automatically grandfathered apps asking for <code>users:read</code> created before January 4th, 2017.</p>
<p>We'd like to complete this transition and remove this grandfathering <strong>entirely</strong> on <strike>August 21, 2018</strike> <strike>October 16, 2018</strike> <strike>a <em>future date</em> we'll one day announce</strike>.</p>
<p>Apps created before January 4th, 2017 with user tokens granted only the <code>users:read</code> scope will no longer receive the <code>email</code> field in user objects.</p>
<p>If you want access to email addresses, you'll need the new <a class="" href=/legacy/legacy-authentication/legacy-oauth-scopes>OAuth permission scope</a>, <code>users:read.email</code>. It provides an explicit, additive way to request access to team email addresses.</p>
<p>Additionally, the <code>bot</code> scope will no longer grant <a class="" href=/legacy/legacy-bot-users>bot user</a> tokens access to email addresses. Bot users must utilize a user token and the <code>users:read.email</code> scope instead.</p>
<p>Don't need access to email address but do need access to user data? <code>users:read</code> should be all you need.</div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class="col col--9"><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/announcement>Announcement</a></ul></div><div class="col text--right col--3"><a aria-label="Read more about Narrowing email access" href=/changelog/2017-04-narrowing-email-access><b>Read more</b></a></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2017/04/01/start-using-rtm-connect-and-stop-using-rtm-start>Start using RTM connect and stop using RTM start</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2017-04-01T00:00:00.000Z>April 1, 2017</time></div></header><div class=markdown><p><strong><em>Update 2017-07-12</em></strong>: As promised, the <code>latest</code> fields within <code>rtm.start</code>'s channel objects are no longer returned. Additionally, the <code>unread_count</code> and <code>unread_count_display</code> channel fields are also <em>missing</em>, though they can still be found in <a class="" href=/reference/methods/conversations.info><code>conversations.info</code></a>.</p>
<hr/>
<p><a class="" href=/reference/methods/rtm.start><code>rtm.start</code></a> began life as a broker and bootstrap to Websocket connections established by Slack's desktop and mobile clients. Whenever our clients needed more information to establish state, those fields would get stuffed into the cacophony that is <code>rtm.start</code>'s opening salvos.</p>
<p>As team sizes and feature complexity has grown, delivering this immense quantity of information about nearly every user, channel, and conversation on a team has become more difficult to compute, consume, or continue.</p>
<p>It is in this spirit we offer a friendlier alternative in <a class="" href=/reference/methods/rtm.connect><code>rtm.connect</code></a>, a method born with the sole purpose of reserving a websocket connection and providing your application its URL.</p>
<p><a class="" href=/reference/methods/rtm.start><code>rtm.start</code></a> must evolve to continue functioning well for all teams and apps. We strongly recommend using <a class="" href=/reference/methods/rtm.connect><code>rtm.connect</code></a> to establish your connections alongside <a class="" href=/reference/methods>Web API methods</a> to build your app's understanding of the users, channels, and conversations within a team.</p>
<p>One such change coming to <code>rtm.start</code> is the elimination of the <code>latest</code> attribute assigned to each <code>channel</code>  in its response.</p>
<p>On <strong>July 11, 2017</strong> we'll no longer return these <code>latest</code> fields. If your app needs a channel's latest timestamp value, use <a class="" href=/reference/methods/conversations.info><code>conversations.info</code></a> to retrieve it instead.</p>
<p>You can test this future behavior in <code>rtm.start</code> today by providing the <code>no_latest=1</code> parameter.</div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class="col col--9"><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/breaking-change>Breaking change</a></ul></div><div class="col text--right col--3"><a aria-label="Read more about Start using RTM connect and stop using RTM start" href=/changelog/2017/04/01/start-using-rtm-connect-and-stop-using-rtm-start><b>Read more</b></a></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2017-02-minor-field-changes>Minor field changes</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2017-02-01T00:00:00.000Z>February 1, 2017</time></div></header><div class=markdown><p>It's almost spring and we're doing a little cleaning early this year.</p>
<p>Ever notice how the <code>username</code> field of a file object in <code>channels.history</code> or [<code>file_shared</code>](/reference/events/file_shared event isn't like typical username fields and contains a bunch of markup usually reserved only for message text?</p>
<p>And why is there a top-level <code>skype</code> field in user profile objects when <em>really</em>, shouldn't that be a custom field?</p>
<p>Well, <em>we've</em> noticed. And so...</div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class="col col--9"><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/announcement>Announcement</a></ul></div><div class="col text--right col--3"><a aria-label="Read more about Minor field changes" href=/changelog/2017-02-minor-field-changes><b>Read more</b></a></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2016/12/31/compilation>2016 shortform changelog entries</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2016-12-31T00:00:00.000Z>December 31, 2016</time></div></header><div class=markdown><h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id=december>December<a href=#december class=hash-link aria-label="Direct link to December" title="Direct link to December" translate=no>​</a></h2>
<ul>
<li class="">Now everyone's bot is present and accounted for. Events API-only bots can toggle online presence by visiting their app management command center. Details worth catching up on: bot user presence.</li>
<li class="">We made it so Slack apps have a profile within Slack like humans do — Here's an <a href=https://twitter.com/SlackAPI/status/809823694683918337 target=_blank rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">announcement tweet</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id=november>November<a href=#november class=hash-link aria-label="Direct link to November" title="Direct link to November" translate=no>​</a></h2>
<ul>
<li class="">Let's extend a warm welcome to new <code>app_id</code> fields now appearing in our APIs. <code>app_id</code> is now found in <code>rtm.start</code> & <code>bots.info</code>. You'll also find <code>app_id</code> in the <code>bot_added</code> & <code>bot_changed</code> events. What's an <code>app_id</code>? It's the alphanumeric string found in the URL bar while managing your Slack apps.</li>
<li class="">We've added a new OAuth permission scope called <code>users:read.email</code>. Apps created after <strong>January 4th, 2017</strong> will need to request this additional scope to gain access to team member <code>email</code> fields when using <code>users.list</code> and <code>users.info</code>. Existing Slack apps with <code>users:read</code> are automatically grandfathered to include these fields.</li>
<li class="">Now you'll find links to practical tutorials and thoughtful articles displayed beside relevant documentation found here on api.slack.com. Discover new articles or browse them by topic in our new Tutorials hub. Written something great? Tell us about it!</li>
<li class="">Our developer relations team has renewed Slack's adoption of key open source tooling: Slack Developer Kits. Discover our Python & node.js SDKs in their new home on our community index.</li>
</ul>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id=october>October<a href=#october class=hash-link aria-label="Direct link to October" title="Direct link to October" translate=no>​</a></h2>
<ul>
<li class="">Your elaborate Slack apps are no longer shackled to but just one team member. Now you can invite other team members to be App Collaborators to share in the fun and responsibility. Here's what our web log has to say about it: <a href=https://medium.com/@SlackAPI/8162e31800f1 target=_blank rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">Build together with App Collaborators</a></li>
</ul>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id=september>September<a href=#september class=hash-link aria-label="Direct link to September" title="Direct link to September" translate=no>​</a></h2>
<ul>
<li class="">We will soon add an additional <code>response_metadata</code> node to our JSON responses; we'll put warnings there first and other useful stuff later. More details are available.</li>
<li class="">Newly issued OAuth token strings are longer than they were before, as we informed you about last month. Let us know if this vexes you.</li>
<li class="">Now you can use the <code>users.profile:write</code> OAuth permission scope to reset and upload profile images using <code>users.deletePhoto</code> and <code>users.setPhoto</code>.</li>
<li class="">We've dramatically improved the process of submitting a Slack App for inclusion in our Slack Marketplace. You'll find a helpful, interactive checklist when first submitting your app. When you're ready to iterate further, you can create a secondary beta application. If a core piece of your app's functionality changes (like requesting new OAuth permission scopes), we'll happily review your app again. <a href=https://medium.com/@SlackAPI/c3234239731#.vwlgf4mwd target=_blank rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">Read all about it</a> on the platform blog.</li>
</ul>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id=august>August<a href=#august class=hash-link aria-label="Direct link to August" title="Direct link to August" translate=no>​</a></h2>
<ul>
<li class="">Ever needed to send a user to Slack directly from your app? Deep link and make native Slack clients part of your app's workflow: Open key teams, channels, and conversations. Or, defer to search results using the slack:// URI scheme.</li>
<li class="">The character length of token strings is getting longer. Find out how long they'll get and how to future-proof yourself for changes in the future.</li>
<li class="">You may encounter an occasional user ID beginning with the letter <code>W</code>. We've released a new version of <a href=https://github.com/slackhq/node-slack-sdk target=_blank rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">node-slack-sdk</a> to correct a related bug.</li>
<li class="">Introducing the Events API, a new way for Slack apps to receive event types previously available only to the real time messaging API. Subscribe to the events your app needs and have them delivered right to your server as they happen. Build a bot or event-driven app without worrying about websockets, and scale it like a web app. <a href=https://medium.com/@SlackAPI/d7120470983f target=_blank rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">Read more</a> about the Events API in our blog post, <a href=https://medium.com/@SlackAPI/d7120470983f target=_blank rel="noopener noreferrer" class=""><em>Subscribe to the Events API</em></a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id=july>July<a href=#july class=hash-link aria-label="Direct link to July" title="Direct link to July" translate=no>​</a></h2>
<ul>
<li class="">Until now, it's been easy to accidentally send messages flush with hundreds of message attachments. We've begun limiting the number of message attachments per message to 100. For approaches like <code>chat.postMessage</code>, incoming webhooks, and <code>chat.update</code>, and <code>response_urls</code> you will receive a <code>too_many_attachments</code> error. Unfortunately, we are unable to serve you an error when sending messages as part of a slash command or message buttons invocation response.</li>
<li class="">If you're interested in listing your Slack app in the Slack Marketplace, you'll want to review our new Slack Marketplace Agreement and consider our Security Review Process. Find these and other policies in our new Slack App developer policy hub.</li>
<li class="">We've corrected a bug where incoming webhooks could post messages in "#general" even 1. if that channel restricts posts and 2. the user owning the webhook was not allowed to post there. This new behavior will only prevent recently created webhooks from posting to restricted "#general" channels, so if your old webhooks are relying on this quirk, they'll be fine for now.</li>
</ul>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id=june>June<a href=#june class=hash-link aria-label="Direct link to June" title="Direct link to June" translate=no>​</a></h2>
<ul>
<li class="">Now your applications can read and write defined team profile fields for individual team members. The <code>users.profile:write</code> scope allows you to edit fields with <code>users.profile.set</code>. The <code>users.profile:read</code> scope empowers you to discover available fields with <code>team.profile.get</code> and retrieve user profiles with <code>users.profile.get</code>.</li>
<li class="">Slack apps can now add action-invoking interactive buttons to messages, allowing you to simplify workflows and encourage users to take decisive action from within Slack.</li>
<li class="">For better readability, syntax highlighting has been added to code blocks throughout our documentation.</li>
<li class="">We've corrected the behavior of <code>stars.list</code> so that it only returns stars belonging to the owner of the presented token. The <code>user</code> parameter may still be used if the provided user ID belongs to the user utilizing the token.</li>
<li class="">Team administrators may now use tokens with the <code>admin</code> scope to request information about the billable status of team members using the team.billableInfo API method.</li>
<li class="">Now that <code>bot_id</code> appears in the real-time messaging API and Web API, you need a better way to look up bot users. Use the new <code>bots.info</code> method to query bot/application information by ID. It requires the <code>users:read</code> scope.</li>
</ul>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id=may>May<a href=#may class=hash-link aria-label="Direct link to May" title="Direct link to May" translate=no>​</a></h2>
<ul>
<li class="">Additional real time messaging API events will begin including the <code>event_ts</code> timestamp field later this summer. Find out what to expect.</li>
<li class="">Now you can put down a footer on your message attachments. Use the <code>footer</code>, <code>footer_icon</code>, and <code>ts</code> fields to tie content across time and space.</li>
<li class="">For the few of you out there using outdated tokens, we've made some changes to authorship behavior when using <code>chat.postMessage</code>.</li>
<li class="">Error conditions in incoming webhooks are due for an improvement. Read all about how blanket HTTP 500s will become more fine-grained, purposeful error conditions. Shipped on <strong>June 16, 2016</strong>.</li>
<li class="">Recently introduced bugs in our iOS & Android apps cause message attachment fields marked as "short" to wrongly render <em>long</em> anyway. Our fixes may take a couple weeks to reach each platform.</li>
<li class="">Sign team members into your website, service, or application with Sign in with Slack, based on the same OAuth 2.0 flow used by the Add to Slack button. Read more about it in this <a href=https://medium.com/slack-developer-blog/introducing-sign-in-with-slack-290949e1c3f5#.hghansb1o target=_blank rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">announcement</a>.</li>
<li class="">We've added two new API methods: <code>users.identity</code> works with Sign in with Slack and <code>auth.revoke</code> revokes hallway privileges for access tokens. Actually, it revokes the whole token.</li>
<li class="">For those who don't know why they should build on Slack: <a href=https://slack.com/developers target=_blank rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">https://slack.com/developers</a></li>
</ul>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id=april>April<a href=#april class=hash-link aria-label="Direct link to April" title="Direct link to April" translate=no>​</a></h2>
<ul>
<li class="">Bot user tokens may now use <code>files.info</code> to look up information about files they have access to by virtue of their channel memberships. Also, very helpful for adapting to upcoming file events changes.</li>
<li class="">Manage your Slack apps joyously with our updated app edit pages.</li>
<li class="">File events are changing in the real time messaging API beginning <strong>May 16th, 2016</strong>. The <code>files.info</code> method is soon to be used by bot users.</li>
<li class="">As <a href=https://medium.com/slack-developer-blog/api-update-new-field-in-api-responses-d23076ea2ef3 target=_blank rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">previously announced</a>, we've added a <code>bot_id</code> field to relevant API responses. Let us know if you run into any issues.</li>
<li class="">We released a family of API methods to create and manage reminders. Meet reminders.list, reminders.info, reminders.add, reminders.delete, and reminders.complete.</li>
<li class="">We fixed an unfortunate bug where a team member could inadvertently uninstall a whole Slack App from their team by removing a single incoming webhook associated with that instance of the app.</li>
<li class="">Find out what we're building! <a href=https://medium.com/slack-developer-blog/the-slack-platform-roadmap-34067b054177 target=_blank rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">Announcing</a> our Platform Roadmap.</li>
<li class="">Another way to keep up with the Slack Platform: Install the API News App to receive occasional, important notifications about the platform.</li>
<li class="">Your bot users author their own messages, now they can edit them too. Bot user tokens may now use <code>chat.update</code>, like humans do.</li>
</ul>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id=march>March<a href=#march class=hash-link aria-label="Direct link to March" title="Direct link to March" translate=no>​</a></h2>
<ul>
<li class="">Now <code>chat.postMessage</code> will better intuit your intent when you don't explicitly specify the <code>as_user</code> parameter. Let us know if we're guessing wrong!</li>
<li class="">One day soon our Web API will warn you when something is only slightly wrong with your requests. Read all about <a href=https://medium.com/slack-developer-blog/well-wishes-and-warnings-in-the-web-api-489456837220 target=_blank rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">API warnings</a>.</li>
<li class=""><em>Be welcoming. Be kind. Look out for each other.</em> This is the Code of Conduct for the Slack Developer community.</li>
<li class="">Now bot users can use methods requiring the <code>dnd:read</code> scope, like <code>dnd.info</code> and <code>dnd.teamInfo</code>. Your bots'll be more polite than a protocol droid!</li>
<li class="">Craft your fancy messages in real time with the new Message Builder!</li>
<li class="">Users can now rename Bot Users they've installed as Slack Apps. More naming, more claiming. No more terrible twos.</li>
<li class="">We <em>finally</em> updated the <a href=https://github.com/slackhq/slack-api-docs target=_blank rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">slackhq/slack-api-docs</a> repository, reflecting recently introduced and quite ancient documentation updates and new features.</li>
</ul>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id=february>February<a href=#february class=hash-link aria-label="Direct link to February" title="Direct link to February" translate=no>​</a></h2>
<ul>
<li class=""><code>reaction_added</code> & <code>reaction_removed</code> events now include an <code>item_user</code> field indicating the user that created the original content everyone's raving about.</li>
<li class="">Published this changelog you're reading right now. So that you can know about all this stuff. Tell your friends.</li>
<li class="">New Web API methods: share files publicly with <code>files.sharedPublicURL</code> or make them private again with <code>files.revokePublicURL</code>.</li>
<li class=""><code>files.comments.add</code>, <code>files.comments.edit</code>, and <code>files.comments.delete</code> are now available to bot users.</li>
<li class="">Quickly find the right tools for your project with our new listing of often-used open source libraries.</li>
<li class="">The handy test token generator previously found in the Web API documentation now stands proud with its very own page.</li>
<li class="">Need help? We have some tips for you.</li>
<li class="">api.slack.com's sidebar is now better organized by topic.</li>
</ul>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id=january>January<a href=#january class=hash-link aria-label="Direct link to January" title="Direct link to January" translate=no>​</a></h2>
<ul>
<li class="">As of <strong>January 4th, 2016</strong>, authorization headers are now required for most Web API requests involving file URLs. See this doc and <a href=https://medium.com/slack-developer-blog/important-changes-to-files-in-the-web-api-eb38f2a9c1e7 target=_blank rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">blog post</a> for more information.</li>
<li class=""><code>url</code> and <code>url_download</code> are no longer part of file objects</li>
<li class="">Enjoy our evolving collection of Frequently Asked Questions (and answers!)</li>
<li class="">Responses to Incoming Webhook requests now include <code>channel_id</code></li>
<li class="">Make sure you're ready before submitting your Slack App for review by following this Slack app checklist.</li>
<li class="">Incoming Webhooks documentation updated to better bait best practices and discourage fishy formatting behavior.</li>
<li class="">The file object documentation now includes a list of possible file types.</li>
</ul></div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class=col><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/compilation>Compilation</a></ul></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2016-11-10-addressing-email-addresses>Addressing email addresses</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2016-11-10T00:00:00.000Z>November 10, 2016</time></div></header><div class=markdown><div class="theme-admonition theme-admonition-warning admonition_xJq3 alert alert--warning"><div class=admonitionHeading_Gvgb><span class=admonitionIcon_Rf37><svg viewBox="0 0 16 16"><path fill-rule=evenodd d="M8.893 1.5c-.183-.31-.52-.5-.887-.5s-.703.19-.886.5L.138 13.499a.98.98 0 0 0 0 1.001c.193.31.53.501.886.501h13.964c.367 0 .704-.19.877-.5a1.03 1.03 0 0 0 .01-1.002L8.893 1.5zm.133 11.497H6.987v-2.003h2.039v2.003zm0-3.004H6.987V5.987h2.039v4.006z"/></svg></span>Accessing Email Addresses</div><div class=admonitionContent_BuS1><p>The<!-- --> <a href=/reference/scopes/users.read.email rel="noopener noreferrer"><code>users:read.email</code></a> <!-- -->OAuth scope is now required to access the <code>email</code> field in user objects returned by the<!-- --> <a href=/reference/methods/users.list><code>users.list</code></a> <!-- -->and<!-- --> <a href=/reference/methods/users.info><code>users.info</code></a> <!-- -->web API methods.<!-- --> <a href=/reference/scopes/users.read><code>users:read</code></a> <!-- -->is no longer a sufficient scope for this data field.<!-- --> <a href=/changelog/2017-04-narrowing-email-access>Learn more</a>.</div></div>
<div class="theme-admonition theme-admonition-warning admonition_xJq3 alert alert--warning"><div class=admonitionHeading_Gvgb><span class=admonitionIcon_Rf37><svg viewBox="0 0 16 16"><path fill-rule=evenodd d="M8.893 1.5c-.183-.31-.52-.5-.887-.5s-.703.19-.886.5L.138 13.499a.98.98 0 0 0 0 1.001c.193.31.53.501.886.501h13.964c.367 0 .704-.19.877-.5a1.03 1.03 0 0 0 .01-1.002L8.893 1.5zm.133 11.497H6.987v-2.003h2.039v2.003zm0-3.004H6.987V5.987h2.039v4.006z"/></svg></span>This original plan has been updated</div><div class=admonitionContent_BuS1><p>Grandfathering is no longer in effect. Please see <a class="" href=/changelog/2017-04-narrowing-email-access>this post from April 2017</a> for more information.</div></div>
<p>We've added a new <a class="" href=/legacy/legacy-authentication/legacy-oauth-scopes>OAuth permission scope</a> called <code>users:read.email</code> and it provides a new explicit, additive way to request access to team email addresses. If you don't need email addresses but do need other user info, <code>users:read</code> is still all you need.</p>
<p>Apps created before <strong>January 4th, 2017</strong> are grandfathered and will continue behaving in a backwards-compatible way. Apps created after that date must request the new <code>users:read.email</code> scope. Regardless of creation date, we encourage all apps to migrate to this new scope.</div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class="col col--9"><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/announcement>Announcement</a></ul></div><div class="col text--right col--3"><a aria-label="Read more about Addressing email addresses" href=/changelog/2016-11-10-addressing-email-addresses><b>Read more</b></a></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2016/09/28/response-metadata-is-on-the-way>Response metadata is on the way</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2016-09-28T00:00:00.000Z>September 28, 2016</time></div></header><div class=markdown><p>We want to tell you even more about your API requests. On November 1st we'll begin including a <code>response_metadata</code> field in HTTP API responses.</p>
<p>At first it will include a <code>warnings</code> array, just as the top-level JSON response does today. API warnings are great example of the kind of information we want to communicate in this response metadata, so please forgive our duplication.</p>
<p>Later we'll include a <code>messages</code> array. It will include human-readable descriptions of errors or warnings generated by your request.</div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class="col col--9"><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/new-feature>New feature</a></ul></div><div class="col text--right col--3"><a aria-label="Read more about Response metadata is on the way" href=/changelog/2016/09/28/response-metadata-is-on-the-way><b>Read more</b></a></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2016/08/23/token-lengthening>Token lengthening</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2016-08-23T00:00:00.000Z>August 23, 2016</time></div></header><div class=markdown><p>Beginning next month, newly issued tokens will be longer than previously issued tokens.</p>
<p>Until now, we haven't documented the string length of tokens, so we hope you've used caution when preparing your token storage apparatuses.</div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class="col col--9"><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/announcement>Announcement</a></ul></div><div class="col text--right col--3"><a aria-label="Read more about Token lengthening" href=/changelog/2016/08/23/token-lengthening><b>Read more</b></a></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2016/08/11/user-id-format-changes>User ID format changes</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2016-08-11T00:00:00.000Z>August 11, 2016</time></div></header><div class=markdown><p>As Slack works to serve the needs of larger businesses by building an enterprise product offering, some aspects of our infrastructure and platform are evolving.</div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class="col col--9"><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/announcement>Announcement</a></ul></div><div class="col text--right col--3"><a aria-label="Read more about User ID format changes" href=/changelog/2016/08/11/user-id-format-changes><b>Read more</b></a></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2016/05/31/more-events-timestamps-in-rtm-api>More event timestamps in the RTM API</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2016-05-31T00:00:00.000Z>May 31, 2016</time></div></header><div class=markdown><p>Within the next few weeks, we'll add <code>event_ts</code> timestamp fields to additional <a class="" href=/reference/events>streamed events</a> you receive in the <a class="" href=/legacy/legacy-rtm-api>real-time messaging API</a>.</p>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id=what-are-these-fields-for>What are these fields for?<a href=#what-are-these-fields-for class=hash-link aria-label="Direct link to What are these fields for?" title="Direct link to What are these fields for?" translate=no>​</a></h2>
<p>The <code>event_ts</code> field differs from the <code>ts</code> timestamp fields you already receive with most events. The <code>ts</code> field is associated with the object or transition the event is describing while the <code>event_ts</code> attribute refers to the streamed event.</p>
<p>The <code>ts</code> field is like a date scrawled on a letter contained within an envelope — it's part of the message itself.</p>
<p>The <code>event_ts</code> is like a postmark stamped on the envelope as part of the postal process, an artifact of the workflow used to deliver the message to the intended recipient.</p>
<p>As with <code>ts</code>, <code>event_ts</code> is expressed in a kind of "<a href=https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unix_time target=_blank rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">epoch time</a>", contained within a string and including fractions of seconds.</p>
<p>An example <code>event_ts</code> timestamp value of <code>"1361482916.000004"</code>, could be converted to UTC as <code>2013-02-21 21:41:56 UTC</code>.</p>
<p><code>event_ts</code> is especially useful when noting your real time progress through a channel's history.</div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class="col col--9"><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/new-feature>New feature</a></ul></div><div class="col text--right col--3"><a aria-label="Read more about More event timestamps in the RTM API" href=/changelog/2016/05/31/more-events-timestamps-in-rtm-api><b>Read more</b></a></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2016/05/19/authorship-changing-for-older-tokens>Authorship changing for older tokens</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2016-05-19T00:00:00.000Z>May 19, 2016</time></div></header><div class=markdown><p>Long ago, a small number of enterprising users and developers scoured through client-side code to discover embedded user tokens and began posting messages and performing other skunkworks operations with them. We applaud this adventurous spirit!</p>
<p>Today we take the first step in retiring usage of these antiquated tokens, by changing their behavior when used to post messages through <a class="" href=/reference/methods/chat.postMessage><code>chat.postMessage</code></a>.</div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class="col col--9"><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/announcement>Announcement</a></ul></div><div class="col text--right col--3"><a aria-label="Read more about Authorship changing for older tokens" href=/changelog/2016/05/19/authorship-changing-for-older-tokens><b>Read more</b></a></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2016-05-17-changes-to-errors-for-incoming-webhooks>Changes to errors for incoming webhooks</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2016-05-17T00:00:00.000Z>May 17, 2016</time></div></header><div class=markdown><p>Today, <a class="" href=/messaging/sending-messages-using-incoming-webhooks>incoming webhooks</a> either work or they don't. Usually they do, but when they don't, you get a somewhat nasty umbrella HTTP 500 error, even when error conditions were due to something well-understood, like malformed requests or non-existent destination channels.</p>
<p>We will diversify our responses to include commonly-interpreted HTTP status codes. For most developers using incoming webhooks, this change will not require additional effort. Most HTTP clients readily consume and predictably react with these status codes.</div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class="col col--9"><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/announcement>Announcement</a></ul></div><div class="col text--right col--3"><a aria-label="Read more about Changes to errors for incoming webhooks" href=/changelog/2016-05-17-changes-to-errors-for-incoming-webhooks><b>Read more</b></a></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2016/04/26/file-events-in-the-rtm-api>RTM API file events payload change</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2016-04-26T00:00:00.000Z>April 26, 2016</time></div></header><div class=markdown><p>If you parse events referencing <a class="" href=/reference/objects/file-object>files</a> in the <a class="" href=/legacy/legacy-rtm-api>real-time messaging API</a>, you may have noticed we send a sometimes comically large packet of information when streaming nearly anything related to a file.</p>
<p>To improve performance and provide a better user experience, we're reducing the payload of most file-related events in the RTM API to include only the file's ID. You'll need to use the <a class="" href=/reference/methods/files.info><code>files.info</code></a> API method to retrieve additional information about files.</p>
<p>These changes will roll out gradually beginning May 16th, 2016 — read below to understand how this change may effect you, especially if you work with bot users.</p>
<p><a class="" href=/legacy/legacy-bot-users>Bot users</a> will gain comparable capabilities, allowing bot user tokens to work with <code>files.info</code> based on the channel memberships and related capabilities granted to them.</div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class="col col--9"><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/announcement>Announcement</a><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/breaking-change>Breaking change</a></ul></div><div class="col text--right col--3"><a aria-label="Read more about RTM API file events payload change" href=/changelog/2016/04/26/file-events-in-the-rtm-api><b>Read more</b></a></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2016/04/14/reminders-api>Reminders API methods</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2016-04-14T00:00:00.000Z>April 14, 2016</time></div></header><div class=markdown><h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id=in-effect-on-april-14-2016>In effect on April 14, 2016<a href=#in-effect-on-april-14-2016 class=hash-link aria-label="Direct link to In effect on April 14, 2016" title="Direct link to In effect on April 14, 2016" translate=no>​</a></h3>
<ul>
<li class="">New <code>reminders</code> API methods for managing reminders in Slack</li>
<li class="">New <code>reminders</code> OAuth scopes for calling the new methods</li>
</ul>
<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id=new-api-methods>New API methods<a href=#new-api-methods class=hash-link aria-label="Direct link to New API methods" title="Direct link to New API methods" translate=no>​</a></h4>
<p>The following API methods have been released, allowing you to programmatically add, remove, and manage reminders.</p>
<ul>
<li class=""><a class="" href=/reference/methods/reminders.add><code>reminders.add</code></a></li>
<li class=""><a class="" href=/reference/methods/reminders.complete><code>reminders.complete</code></a></li>
<li class=""><a class="" href=/reference/methods/reminders.delete><code>reminders.delete</code></a></li>
<li class=""><a class="" href=/reference/methods/reminders.info><code>reminders.info</code></a></li>
<li class=""><a class="" href=/reference/methods/reminders.list><code>reminders.list</code></a></li>
</ul>
<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id=new-oauth-scopes>New OAuth scopes<a href=#new-oauth-scopes class=hash-link aria-label="Direct link to New OAuth scopes" title="Direct link to New OAuth scopes" translate=no>​</a></h4>
<p>The following OAuth scopes will grant you access to the new methods listed above:</p>
<ul>
<li class=""><a class="" href=/reference/scopes/reminders.read><code>reminders:read</code></a></li>
<li class=""><a class="" href=/reference/scopes/reminders.write><code>reminders:write</code></a></li>
</ul></div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class=col><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/new-feature>New feature</a></ul></div></footer></article><article class=margin-bottom--xl><header><h2 class=title_f1Hy><a href=/changelog/2015/12/31/compilation>2015 shortform changelog entries</a></h2><div class="container_mt6G margin-vert--md"><time datetime=2015-12-31T00:00:00.000Z>December 31, 2015</time></div></header><div class=markdown><h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id=november>November<a href=#november class=hash-link aria-label="Direct link to November" title="Direct link to November" translate=no>​</a></h2>
<ul>
<li class="">
<p>More granular OAuth scopes are here! Now your apps can ask for the exact level of access you need.</p>
</li>
<li class="">
<p>Added authorization support for thumbnail URLs appearing in File objects.</p>
</li>
<li class="">
<p>Added <code>team.integrationLogs</code> to the Web API</p>
</li>
<li class="">
<p>Announced <a href=https://medium.com/slack-developer-blog/important-changes-to-files-in-the-web-api-eb38f2a9c1e7 target=_blank rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">important changes</a> to the Files methods of the Web API.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id=december>December<a href=#december class=hash-link aria-label="Direct link to December" title="Direct link to December" translate=no>​</a></h2>
<ul>
<li class="">
<p>Now you can upgrade your Slack App's OAuth Scopes by managing your apps. <a href=https://medium.com/slack-developer-blog/how-to-upgrade-your-slack-oauth-scopes-96f1eb6e5bc8 target=_blank rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">This article</a> explains it all.</p>
</li>
<li class="">
<p>Don't press snooze until you've dreamed about our new Do Not Disturb Web API methods.</p>
</li>
<li class="">
<p>You can now package Bot Users within Slack Apps, making your creations easier to distribute to teams.</p>
</li>
<li class="">
<p>We launched the <a class="" href=/slack-marketplace>Slack Marketplace</a>, where teams can discover apps like yours.</p>
</li>
<li class="">
<p>We <a href=https://medium.com/slack-developer-blog/launch-platform-114754258b91 target=_blank rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">announced the Slack Fund</a> to "give developers the backing they need to build everything possible in Slack."</p>
</li>
<li class="">
<p>The api.slack.com home page is fancier.</p>
</li>
<li class="">
<p>Enjoy major updates to the Slash Commands documentation, expanding on topics like...</p>
</li>
<li class="">
<p>...delayed responses.</p>
</li>
</ul></div><footer class="row docusaurus-mt-lg"><div class=col><b>Tags:</b><ul class="tags_jXut padding--none margin-left--sm"><li class=tag_QGVx><a rel=tag class="tag_zVej tagRegular_sFm0" href=/changelog/tags/compilation>Compilation</a></ul></div></footer></article><nav class=pagination-nav aria-label="Blog list page navigation"></nav></main></div></div></div><footer class="theme-layout-footer footer"><div class="container container-fluid"><div class="row footer__links"><div class="theme-layout-footer-column col footer__col"><div class=footer__title>.</div><ul class="footer__items clean-list"><li class=footer__item>
